# Machine Learning and AI Foundations: Producing Explainable AI (XAI) and Interpretable Machine Learning Solutions

> Data scientists and machine learning professionals have to stay apace with the latest techniques and approaches in the field. In this course, instructor Keith McCormick shows you how to produce explainable AI (XAI) and interpretable machine learning (IML) solutions.Learn why the need for XAI has been rapidly increasing in recent years. Explore available methods and common techniques for XAI and IM

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions) | 2h 14m | Intermediate | 36K learners
> [Jump to Path Context ↓](#path-context)

## Table of Contents

### Chapter Overview

- **1. Introduction** (3 videos)
- **2. 1. What Are XAI and IML?** (7 videos)
- **3. 2. Why Isolating a Variable’s Contribution Is Difficult** (3 videos)
- **4. 3. Black Box Model 101** (4 videos)
- **5. 4. Introduction to KNIME for XAI and IML** (4 videos)
- **6. 5. XAI Techniques: Global Explanations** (5 videos)
- **7. 6. Techniques for Local Explanations** (6 videos)
- **8. 7. IML Techniques** (3 videos)
- **9. Conclusion** (1 videos)

### 2. 1. What Are XAI and IML?

#### Understanding the what and why your models predict
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=0)** - In an article in "Harvard Data Science Review", "Should We Trust Algorithms?", the author shares a slightly humorous yet powerful story of what issues can arise with computer predictions.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=13)** When negotiating the narrow streets in the ancient university town of Coimbra, the GPS confidently told us to go left, and so we obeyed her, but we were somewhat taken aback, when the road abruptly turned into steps.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=30)** We stopped in time, but after that, we were not so trusting.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=34)** Since it didn't end in disaster, I think we can appreciate the everyday reality of AI models making mistakes, and can probably think of humorous times that our smart devices at home misunderstood what music we were requesting or what word we were pronouncing.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=52)** I share this story because it raises three issues that we will be revisiting again and again.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=58)** Is the model transparent?
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=60)** Is the reason for a specific individual prediction transparent?
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=65)** Is it high stakes?
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=67)** XAI or explainable AI is a set of techniques to explain a model's prediction even when the nature of the modeling algorithm would normally make this difficult.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=79)** XAI is the primary subject of this course.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=83)** Why would explanations be so difficult?
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=86)** Commonly, it's the very nature of the technique.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=90)** For instance, deep neural networks are very complex models that are difficult to interpret.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=97)** But even traditional neural networks, back when they had just one hidden layer, were already difficult to interpret.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=105)** Other popular techniques like XGBoost or support vector machines would also fall into this category.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=112)** In the case of the nearly averted car accident, the prediction itself was clear, "take a left," but why it made an error was not so clear.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=123)** Whether it is high stakes, is somewhat subjective, but they narrowly avoided an accident.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=129)** It wasn't just that they got caught up in traffic, so I think most would consider it high stakes.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=136)** When we are trusting AI and machine learning to make decisions for us, these are all important issues.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=142)** If the prediction being made is whether or not to buy a pair of shoes or adopt a particular clothing style, we want accuracy, but we're probably willing to sacrifice transparency.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=155)** We are also probably fairly patient with search engine results.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=159)** Maybe the first choice isn't that great, but as long as what we're searching for is on the first page, we likely move along without much of a thought.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=169)** Even if we're curious, we don't urgently need to know why the top choice was not optimal.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=176)** If, on the other hand, the problem is high stakes, like getting a favorable rate on a loan, or perhaps even being turned down for a loan, we very much want transparency.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=188)** Frankly, if our business operates in a regulatory environment like insurance or banking, we are likely forced to have transparency.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=199)** There will be government agencies that require justification for different prices or justification for decisions like denying an insurance claim.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=210)** This course is about these issues, specifically when we do need transparency into why a model made a particular prediction, how do we go about providing that transparency?
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=225)** The techniques for revealing the inner workings of predictive models, is a complex and evolving world as AI and machine learning techniques get increasingly diverse and complex.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=237)** While XAI will be our primary focus, we will explore two distinct approaches and world views.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=245)** First, XAI, where so called black box models are built yet additional steps are taken to explain them, but also the other approach, interpretable machine learning, where you choose to build a transparent model from the start.
>
> **[4:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/understanding-the-what-and-why-your-models-predict?u=76281980&t=261)** We will be exploring both, and rehearsing how to perform each approach step by step.

#### Variable importance and reason codes
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/variable-importance-and-reason-codes?u=76281980)

>

#### Comparing IML and XAI
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/comparing-iml-and-xai?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/comparing-iml-and-xai?u=76281980&t=9)** Let's start by discussing the explainable AI approach in more detail.

>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/comparing-iml-and-xai?u=76281980&t=60)** This is also true of the loans and reason codes that we discussed in the previous video.

>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/comparing-iml-and-xai?u=76281980&t=72)** We want to use these opaque models for their accuracy, but when we do, we sacrifice transparency.

>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/comparing-iml-and-xai?u=76281980&t=126)** Since these additional analyses are done after the model is built, they are often described as post hoc explanations.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/comparing-iml-and-xai?u=76281980&t=135)** In this course, we'll explain various methods for doing this, and then we'll look at how to create these explanations in the KNIME analytics platform.

>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/comparing-iml-and-xai?u=76281980&t=149)** Traditional machine warning techniques like decision trees are inherently explainable and interpretable.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/comparing-iml-and-xai?u=76281980&t=155)** It is in the very nature of the technique that you can get a fairly detailed accounting of why particular predictions are made, although, you have to be careful to double check how various experts use the term.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/comparing-iml-and-xai?u=76281980&t=170)** We'll use the term interpretable machine learning for building machine learning models that are interpretable, because the algorithm that was chosen results in a transparent model.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/comparing-iml-and-xai?u=76281980&t=184)** I've also encountered this described as intrinsic interpretability, which really just means self-explanatory, but will stick to the term interpretable machine learning.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/comparing-iml-and-xai?u=76281980&t=195)** In addition to decision trees, techniques like linear regression and logistic regression, among others, fall into this category.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/comparing-iml-and-xai?u=76281980&t=205)** Some modelers worry that it implies that we have to fall back on techniques that haven't changed in decades.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/comparing-iml-and-xai?u=76281980&t=213)** Frankly, that's okay, because sometimes the older techniques are just fine, but interpretable machine learning doesn't force you to use techniques that might seem out of date, or that fail to be cutting edge.
>
> **[3:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/comparing-iml-and-xai?u=76281980&t=227)** Some researchers have recognized the importance of having inherently interpretable techniques, and they're working on powerful modern algorithms for doing so.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/comparing-iml-and-xai?u=76281980&t=236)** Some of these researchers have adopted an almost contrarian point of view, voicing the opinion that we rush to black box models and XAI too quickly.
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/comparing-iml-and-xai?u=76281980&t=247)** So in this course, we'll acknowledge that black box models are an important part of machine learning, and we want to present you with options for both explainable AI, as well as interpretable machine learning.

> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=195)** And the error rate is now so low that it has plateaued and is now better than human accuracy.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=204)** There are two additional elements that are present in the contemporary machine learning community that are putting additional pressure on those of us as data scientists to adopt black box techniques.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=219)** One is AutoML, and another is Kaggle.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=224)** Automated machine learning tools feature what one might call a tournament of algorithms where numerous algorithms compete and either a single winner is chosen or sometimes a team of multiple winners are used in a combined model.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=241)** In other words, an ensemble.
>
> **[4:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=244)** Kaggle competitions typically award a monetary prize, so some objective criteria needs to be used.
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=253)** And accuracy is calculated to multiple decimal places.
>
> **[4:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=258)** These competitions have created a venue for a whole generation of data scientists to learn and to demonstrate their knowledge.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=267)** So this is very positive overall, but it can create behaviors that are rather different than what you would see in the workplace.
>
> **[4:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=277)** And it puts pressure on competitors to increase model complexity, even if it's only for very modest gains.
>
> **[4:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=286)** Meanwhile, in the world of decision trees, a related transformation has been going on.
>
> **[4:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=293)** Decision tree models have also been becoming increasingly complex.
>
> **[4:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=299)** Single trees are rare complex enough to win these machine learning competitions.
>
> **[5:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=306)** It's almost always ensembles of trees.
>
> **[5:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=310)** Ensembles can be very powerful.
>
> **[5:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=313)** Ensembles are a combination of any kind of model, but typically trees are the most common component model.
>
> **[5:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=322)** I have an entire course dedicated to using this technique successfully, but the very large number of component models makes interpretation virtually impossible.
>
> **[5:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=336)** In short, while the component trees may be transparent, the resulting ensemble is not.
>
> **[5:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=344)** These parallel trends are making opaque models more common than ever.
>
> **[5:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=350)** They absolutely dominate certain application areas, and they also dominate data science instruction.
>
> **[5:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=358)** But there's a cost.
>
> **[6:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=360)** We now have a large number of these opaque models, but our need for transparency has not gone away.
>
> **[6:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/trends-in-ai-making-the-xai-problem-more-prominent?u=76281980&t=368)** So as opaque models are trending, it also results in the rise of importance of our subject, XAI.

#### XAI for debugging models
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/xai-for-debugging-models?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/xai-for-debugging-models?u=76281980&t=12)** In a recent interview, Marco Ribeiro tells a compelling story.

>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/xai-for-debugging-models?u=76281980&t=26)** He explains that he didn't set out to study XAI at first.

>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/xai-for-debugging-models?u=76281980&t=45)** The researcher and academic Cynthia Rudin, a name we hear repeatedly in this course, often refers to a similar case study.

>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/xai-for-debugging-models?u=76281980&t=65)** Both of these examples are a reminder that cross-validation alone is not sufficient to protect us if something about the data collection or data preparation impacts both our training data and our testing data.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/xai-for-debugging-models?u=76281980&t=82)** We need another layer of protection.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/xai-for-debugging-models?u=76281980&t=85)** We need a way to detect if something like this might be happening.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/xai-for-debugging-models?u=76281980&t=89)** We also need to know how to improve our model with real-world human expertise, both of which are difficult if the model is opaque.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/xai-for-debugging-models?u=76281980&t=100)** If you are already actively building machine learning models you've likely heard stories like this, or have had experiences like this yourself.

>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/xai-for-debugging-models?u=76281980&t=119)** This isn't just about meeting an external requirement.
>

### 3. 2. Why Isolating a Variable’s Contribution Is Difficult

#### Challenges of variable attribution with linear regression
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/challenges-of-variable-attribution-with-linear-regression?u=76281980)

> **[7:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/challenges-of-variable-attribution-with-linear-regression?u=76281980&t=472)** The point is, if you run just one model, it's the most accurate model.
>
> **[7:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/challenges-of-variable-attribution-with-linear-regression?u=76281980&t=477)** If you think it's the model that you to go with, you might not be attending to these changes.
>

> **[8:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/challenges-of-variable-attribution-with-linear-regression?u=76281980&t=489)** So what do we conclude?
>
> **[8:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/challenges-of-variable-attribution-with-linear-regression?u=76281980&t=491)** Well, when we report something that has such great interest to our colleagues, clients, and management, like variables are most important, it's a fundamental thing that everybody wants to know, we have to tread carefully.
>
> **[8:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/challenges-of-variable-attribution-with-linear-regression?u=76281980&t=507)** Even with the simplest models, we should examine more than one model and consider more than one method of measuring variable importance.

>
> **[8:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/challenges-of-variable-attribution-with-linear-regression?u=76281980&t=519)** To use some of the explainability techniques even when we're using a transparent model, like multiple linear regression.

#### Rashomon effect
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] So you've built your model and you're listing your input variables in order of importance.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=8)** You're excited to share this information with the team.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=11)** And then you wonder, you almost went with a different model.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=16)** You tried lots of different models.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=18)** And the one that was second in terms of accuracy was nearly as good a performer.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=24)** What if you had gone with the other model?
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=27)** Would this list of the most important variables be similar or perhaps rather different?
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=33)** The name Rashmon comes originally from a famous mid-century Japanese movie by Akira Kurosawa.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=40)** In the film, four different witnesses describe a murder, but with differing and often contradictory details.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=49)** It's become a metaphor for different points of view.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=53)** The use of Rashmon as a metaphor in machine learning comes from a very influential paper by Leo Breiman.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=60)** "The Two Cultures".
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=62)** Leo Breiman was a brilliant innovator that along with others brought us techniques like CART and Random Forest.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=70)** He writes, "different models, all of them equally good, may give different pictures of the relation between the predictor and response variables."
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=82)** "The question of which one most accurately reflects the data is difficult to resolve."
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=90)** Cynthia Rudin of Duke University and her colleagues have taken this one step further and introduced the idea of a Rashmon set, which they define in this way, "The set of prediction models that provide near-optimal accuracy."
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=106)** In other words, there's more than one, so collectively, they form a set that together are all near the top in terms of performance.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=116)** Why is this important?
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=117)** Well, it seems to undermine our ability to figure out what's important, which is such a fundamental question that we need to ask.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=125)** "Existing variable importance measures do not generally account for the fact that many prediction models may fit the data almost equally well."
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=136)** Rudin and her co-authors continue, "In such cases, the model used by one analyst may rely on entirely different covariate information than the model used by another analyst."
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=152)** Wow, so you think you figured out variable importance, but if you had chosen a different model, the list might have been entirely different.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=161)** In the paper, they even propose an algorithmic approach to address this called model class reliance, but short of implementing their algorithm, there is some general advice that we can explore right now.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=176)** First, awareness helps.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=178)** Now that you've heard about this problem, you'll start to perceive it more readily.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=184)** Where you really get in trouble is when you're highly confident that you figured it all out and then you're contradicted later.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=192)** Awareness will make you more cautious and less likely to do that.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=197)** Second, run variable importance on more than one model.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=201)** Be extremely careful about picking a single most accurate model running variable importance on it, assuming that it's a stable and accurate list and immediately writing a key driver analysis to management.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=216)** If the list is unstable, and you give different advice later, it will be confusing to everyone.
>
> **[3:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=222)** Frankly, including yourself.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=225)** If the top three performing models are very similar, then you're on more solid ground.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=231)** Next, perform good variable reduction.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=234)** The reason is is that this Rashmon phenomenon tends to be more pronounced and produce more instability when you have lots of very similar inputs competing with each other for the same variants.
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=248)** You want to remove some of that redundancy and I find that this helps.
>
> **[4:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=254)** Finally, always include a transparent model in the mix.
>
> **[4:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=260)** If all of the models that you've tried are black box, you've got less context.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=267)** Even if the transparent model is less accurate, at least you've got some options to compare.
>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/rashomon-effect?u=76281980&t=273)** So the Rashmon effect is very real, now that you're aware of it, you'll perceive it, but there some things you can do.

>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-qualifies-as-a-black-box?u=76281980&t=97)** Traditional machine warning algorithms are usually considered as automatically belonging in the transparent model category.

>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-qualifies-as-a-black-box?u=76281980&t=115)** First, of course, are those complex models deriving from black box algorithms, but also models with large numbers of inputs.

>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-qualifies-as-a-black-box?u=76281980&t=133)** And that should probably be considered a black box model as well.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-qualifies-as-a-black-box?u=76281980&t=138)** Finally, as we've just seen, if a model is proprietary, and you're not allowed reveal the model details in their entirety, you likely still need something, like the reason codes that we explored earlier in the course.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-qualifies-as-a-black-box?u=76281980&t=153)** So in all three of these situations, you may find that providing transparency becomes a challenge, and therefore, in all three situations, you might want to consider some of the techniques that we will be seeing in this course.

#### What is the accuracy interpretability tradeoff?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] So what exactly is this accuracy interpretability trade-off?
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=6)** Well, on the internet, you'll find dozens and dozens of charts like this one, but it's not always clear exactly what is being measured on the x and y-axis.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=19)** It's mostly just being asserted to be true.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=24)** One fact of agreement to everyone, and it certainly is true, is that linear regression belongs in the upper left corner and deep learning belongs in the lower right.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=36)** However, it's rarely clear in blog posts or in videos you may find whether the author did some kind of experiment or if they're attempting to generalize.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=48)** However, if you want a serious discussion of this, and it definitely is a real phenomenon, it's hard to improve upon the extremely influential book "Introduction to Statistical Learning" by two giants of the field, Hastie and Tibshirani, and their coauthors.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=68)** Hastie has a website supporting the book that you see here, and he also makes the book available as a download.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=77)** The relevant figure for us is figure 2.7.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=82)** And you can see that they've labeled this a little bit differently.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=86)** They've labeled the x-axis flexibility and the y-axis interpretability, and in the chapter in which you find this figure, they talk at length about what is called the bias variance trade-off.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=102)** I invest multiple videos in this whole concept and discuss it in detail in my Introduction to Classification course.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=111)** And Hastie and Tibshirani in the book make a much more careful argument than what you might find in those charts on the web that I just referenced.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=121)** So the basics are almost universally agreed upon, so let's talk about those now.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=129)** So rather than generalizing, we can be more specific.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=132)** A couple of facts are absolutely true, and there's no debate.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=137)** A polynomial regression is always more flexible, as Hastie and Tibshirani define it, than a linear regression.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=145)** If you're looking at a scatterplot, it is quite literally true.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=149)** The polynomial regression can bend, demonstrating its flexibility.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=154)** So r squared will always go up.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=157)** That's just a fact.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=158)** A complex tree is more flexible than a sparse tree, meaning if you grow a decision tree an additional branch, accuracy is going to go up, and flexibility's going to go up.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=171)** That is also without debate.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=173)** So therefore, what Hastie and Tibshirani are trying to show in that figure, figure 2.7, is that more complex is associated with more flexible, as they define it and as I've begun to describe to you.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=189)** However, this is where it becomes a little bit more subtle, and there's a little room for debate.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=195)** Is flexible always better?
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=199)** If you're simply talking about interpretability and accuracy, I think most people immediately draw the conclusion, "Wow, I want more accurate.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=208)** I'll deal with interpretability later."
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=211)** But, again, the argument is more subtle.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=213)** Is flexible always better?
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=215)** Well, right in the book, Hastie and Tibshirani talk about circumstances where you might sacrifice flexibility for interpretability, really the theme of a big section of this course when we're going to talk about interpretable machine learning.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=231)** But the other issue is it's one thing to show that you always get increased accuracy on training data.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=240)** And when you start to talk about evaluation and when you start to talk about user testing and applying these models in the real world, it's not always true that flexible is always better.
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=253)** So remember this trade-off because you're not forced to go black box and then explain it.
>
> **[4:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-is-the-accuracy-interpretability-tradeoff?u=76281980&t=260)** You'll have to on an individual, project-by-project basis try to navigate the trade-off between these different choices.

#### The argument against XAI
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/the-argument-against-xai?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/the-argument-against-xai?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The first time I encountered the ideas of Cynthia Rudin, I was attending her keynote at the 2019 Knowledge Discovery in Databases conference in Anchorage, Alaska.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/the-argument-against-xai?u=76281980&t=14)** The premise of her keynote was perhaps we're using complicated models when we don't need them.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/the-argument-against-xai?u=76281980&t=22)** You can find her keynote on the internet, and I highly recommend it.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/the-argument-against-xai?u=76281980&t=26)** She's become very vocal, and she's taken a strong contrarian position on explainable AI, but she's very well regarded.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/the-argument-against-xai?u=76281980&t=35)** She recently won a million-dollar award for pioneering work in socially responsible AI.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/the-argument-against-xai?u=76281980&t=43)** I'd like to briefly summarize the key points of her position.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/the-argument-against-xai?u=76281980&t=47)** If you're curious to learn more, she's prolific, so it's easy to find articles and presentations where she discusses these points in more detail.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/the-argument-against-xai?u=76281980&t=57)** She and her graduate students have also made a number of technical contributions to the field, some of which we'll see later in the course.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/the-argument-against-xai?u=76281980&t=65)** First, she argues that accuracy is rarely a good argument for building a more complex model.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/the-argument-against-xai?u=76281980&t=74)** She believes that the accuracy complexity argument is exaggerated, or perhaps even false.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/the-argument-against-xai?u=76281980&t=79)** Her reasoning is that even if theory tells us that complex models are better, when you actually do this work in practice, opaque models are rarely substantially better.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/the-argument-against-xai?u=76281980&t=91)** This is something that I've seen in my own work, so you want to be careful and thoughtful when making the choice to build an opaque model.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/the-argument-against-xai?u=76281980&t=99)** She also argues that black box models can be harmful.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/the-argument-against-xai?u=76281980&t=103)** They can be wrong, and then no one knows, and if you don't understand them, you also can't use subject matter expertise to make them better.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/the-argument-against-xai?u=76281980&t=112)** Next, and perhaps here she's being even a bit more controversial, she argues that opaque models are easier to keep proprietary, therefore, there is perhaps a financial interest in either using black box models, or keeping transparent models secret.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/the-argument-against-xai?u=76281980&t=130)** Finally, she passionately argues that the field should be more focused on advancing interpretable machine learning, where she's made some advances herself, and not being so focused on XAI.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/the-argument-against-xai?u=76281980&t=146)** Her position, in summary, is to consider using interpretable machine learning from the start, and then you don't need explanation.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/the-argument-against-xai?u=76281980&t=156)** We're taking the position in this course that black box techniques in interpretable machine learning are going to coexist for the foreseeable future.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/the-argument-against-xai?u=76281980&t=166)** So explaining black box models is better than not explaining them, but it's helpful to be reminded that we almost always have a choice.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/the-argument-against-xai?u=76281980&t=175)** We'll have more to say about interpretable machine learning later in the course.

#### Using surrogate models for global explanations
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-surrogate-models-for-global-explanations?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-surrogate-models-for-global-explanations?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] A surrogate model is simply a substitute.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-surrogate-models-for-global-explanations?u=76281980&t=4)** When you feel that your project is best served by a black box model, you can build a second model that explains the first.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-surrogate-models-for-global-explanations?u=76281980&t=15)** Here's the key difference.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-surrogate-models-for-global-explanations?u=76281980&t=17)** Your target variable changes.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-surrogate-models-for-global-explanations?u=76281980&t=20)** Your new target variable is the output of the first model.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-surrogate-models-for-global-explanations?u=76281980&t=27)** In his excellent book, "Interpretable Machine Learning: A Guide for Making Black Box Models Explainable," which I highly recommend by the way, Christoff Molnar outlines the generic steps in more detail than I will here.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-surrogate-models-for-global-explanations?u=76281980&t=41)** We will do the bare minimum at first.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-surrogate-models-for-global-explanations?u=76281980&t=44)** A bit later, we'll learn that KNIME can help us with surrogate models.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-surrogate-models-for-global-explanations?u=76281980&t=50)** So the first step is to get the predictions from the black box model, then train an interpretable model on the predictions, meaning that the predictions of first model become the dependent variable of the second model, then measure how well it replicates.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-surrogate-models-for-global-explanations?u=76281980&t=70)** When we do the demonstration in KNIME, we're going to skip this step to keep it simple.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-surrogate-models-for-global-explanations?u=76281980&t=76)** By the way, it is okay if the surrogate model is a bit over fit, because the nature of the model is quite different.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-surrogate-models-for-global-explanations?u=76281980&t=87)** A lot of the noise has been worked out of the system with the first model.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-surrogate-models-for-global-explanations?u=76281980&t=94)** It's quite common that the accuracy on the second model is quite high and a bit over fit.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-surrogate-models-for-global-explanations?u=76281980&t=101)** Finally, you have to interpret the model, which we'll practice in the demonstration.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-surrogate-models-for-global-explanations?u=76281980&t=106)** So let's proceed into KNIME and see how this all works.

#### Permutation feature importance
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/permutation-feature-importance?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/permutation-feature-importance?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Now let's talk about permutation feature importance.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/permutation-feature-importance?u=76281980&t=5)** The basic idea is straightforward enough but the method might surprise you at first.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/permutation-feature-importance?u=76281980&t=11)** To test the importance of a feature we're going to shuffle that one column.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/permutation-feature-importance?u=76281980&t=18)** What the shuffling does is break the relationship that is present between the feature and the target variable.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/permutation-feature-importance?u=76281980&t=25)** That's the permutation in the name.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/permutation-feature-importance?u=76281980&t=28)** So if the variable was helpful, the error rate will go up in a measurable way.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/permutation-feature-importance?u=76281980&t=35)** And if the variable's not so helpful the error rate is not going to change.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/permutation-feature-importance?u=76281980&t=41)** Once again we have Bryman and Rudin to thank once more for various contributions and Molnar is a great source on this topic as well.

### 7. 6. Techniques for Local Explanations

#### Developing an intuition for Shapley values
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/developing-an-intuition-for-shapley-values?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/developing-an-intuition-for-shapley-values?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Shapley values are a popular way of doing local explanations that originated in game theory, and they're implemented in KNIME.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/developing-an-intuition-for-shapley-values?u=76281980&t=9)** I'd like to illustrate Shapley values with a story.

> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/developing-an-intuition-for-shapley-values?u=76281980&t=246)** I hope you found that fun, but also helpful in trying to understand what KNIME is doing when it's figuring out the contribution, not of the three friends, but of all the variables in your model.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/developing-an-intuition-for-shapley-values?u=76281980&t=259)** But keep in mind, if you had 20 or 50 or 100 variables, this would get complicated real fast.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/developing-an-intuition-for-shapley-values?u=76281980&t=267)** So this is an easy way to develop just an intuition for what Shapley values are all about.

#### Introducing SHAP
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/introducing-shap?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/introducing-shap?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] While Shapley values have been borrowed from game theory, there is a much younger concept based on Shapley values but that was specifically developed for XAI SHAP.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/introducing-shap?u=76281980&t=13)** First, the acronym, it stands for shapely additive explanations and was proposed by Scott Lundberg and his co-authors.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/introducing-shap?u=76281980&t=23)** We don't need to get deep into the math.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/introducing-shap?u=76281980&t=26)** For our purposes, it will be sufficient to review just a couple of high level points.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/introducing-shap?u=76281980&t=32)** First, an explicit goal of SHAP is to try to perform these calculations faster.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/introducing-shap?u=76281980&t=37)** The Shapley value algorithm is not very scalable.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/introducing-shap?u=76281980&t=41)** Next SHAP attempts to explain the delta or difference between a case and a base rate.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/introducing-shap?u=76281980&t=49)** Remember that we are using SHAP for local explanations.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/introducing-shap?u=76281980&t=53)** So we're not trying to explain the whole model.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/introducing-shap?u=76281980&t=55)** So what we care about is explaining how each variable moves a particular case higher or lower than the group.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/introducing-shap?u=76281980&t=64)** We're trying to answer, for instance, why Anne's credit risk might be lower than the average credit risk.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/introducing-shap?u=76281980&t=72)** Next, the contributions are additive.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/introducing-shap?u=76281980&t=74)** Some inputs will bring Anne's risk higher and others will bring her risk lower.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/introducing-shap?u=76281980&t=80)** But when you add them all up we should return earn to that delta value.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/introducing-shap?u=76281980&t=84)** The difference between her risk and the baseline risk.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/introducing-shap?u=76281980&t=88)** One caution, there's more than one kind of SHAP.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/introducing-shap?u=76281980&t=92)** We'll only be discussing SHAP as it's supported in nine.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/introducing-shap?u=76281980&t=96)** But if you get deeper into the subject you'll find that there's more than one flavor of it out there.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/introducing-shap?u=76281980&t=101)** That's just a quick overview, but that will be enough to help you interpret SHAP values in nine.
