#### Using LIME to provide local explanations for neural networks
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-lime-to-provide-local-explanations-for-neural-networks?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-lime-to-provide-local-explanations-for-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Our next technique, LIME, is also quite new and specifically developed for XAI.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-lime-to-provide-local-explanations-for-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=8)** The acronym stands for Local Interpretable Model-Agnostic Explanations.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-lime-to-provide-local-explanations-for-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=16)** LIME was developed by Marco Rivera and his coauthors.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-lime-to-provide-local-explanations-for-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=21)** The concept is more important than the math at this point.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-lime-to-provide-local-explanations-for-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=25)** So let's review the logic behind LIME.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-lime-to-provide-local-explanations-for-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=28)** First, it's safe to assume that you felt you needed a complex model.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-lime-to-provide-local-explanations-for-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=34)** To be clear, LIME is model-agnostic.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-lime-to-provide-local-explanations-for-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=37)** So the approach can be used with any model, but if you found a way to build a simpler model, presumably you would have just deployed the simpler model.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-lime-to-provide-local-explanations-for-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=49)** So if you felt forced to go with a rather complex model, let's say a very large and deep decision tree.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-lime-to-provide-local-explanations-for-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=57)** How were you going to build a simple surrogate that is faithful, to use a phrase that the authors often use, faithful to the original?
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-lime-to-provide-local-explanations-for-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=68)** Well, here's the solution that the authors came up with.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-lime-to-provide-local-explanations-for-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=71)** Don't try to build a surrogate globally, build a surrogate locally.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-lime-to-provide-local-explanations-for-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=78)** Concentrate only on cases near and thereby similar to the case that you're trying to describe.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-lime-to-provide-local-explanations-for-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=86)** LIME samples nearby cases, then weights closer cases more heavily.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-lime-to-provide-local-explanations-for-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=92)** Remember, we are doing local explanations, so we're focused on a single target case.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-lime-to-provide-local-explanations-for-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=99)** Closer cases simply means closer to the case we're trying to explain.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-lime-to-provide-local-explanations-for-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=106)** Another reason that the concept is more important than the algorithmic details, is that there's more than one way to do this.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-lime-to-provide-local-explanations-for-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=115)** For instance, as we shall see, NIME's local explanation view also samples near the target case, but defines this local neighborhood using a slightly different algorithm than LIME.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/using-lime-to-provide-local-explanations-for-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=130)** Nonetheless, LIME and the concept behind it has become one of the most influential and frequently mentioned local explanation techniques in XAI.

> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/what-are-counterfactuals?u=76281980&t=114)** We saw this kind of thing in our visit to the credit simulator website earlier in the course.

> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/knime-s-local-explanation-view-node?u=76281980&t=67)** And the reason that that's important is, remember that we're doing local explanations.

>

### 8. 7. IML Techniques

#### General advice for better IML
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] A premise of this course has been that complex black box models are here to stay, but interpretable models are also here to stay.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=8)** Working directly with interpretable models can often be your best choice, but mastering interpretable models draws upon all the modeling skills that you develop over a career.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=20)** Nonetheless, there are some general principles we can discuss at this point in our journey that seem especially suited to this course.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=28)** Where I see folks get into trouble is that they sometimes skip data assessment and data prep and jump immediately to their favorite black box algorithm without trying anything else first.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=41)** That strategy makes it nearly impossible to know if you're on the right or wrong track and if you've successfully avoided perennial problems like data quality issues or overfitting.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=53)** Always try interpretable models first so that you can learn from your data and from your initial attempts.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=61)** Then you also know the accuracy score that you need to beat and whether sacrificing interpretability is worth it.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=69)** Also, it's impossible to do more traditional methods well without feature engineering.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=77)** This can get a bit tricky because you may end up with multiple datasets.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=82)** That happens because each of the traditional algorithms that you use might need slightly different data prep.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=88)** Some techniques need this attention more than others, but without feature engineering, you aren't giving the interpretable models a fair shot.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=98)** We'll have more to say about this in the next video.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=101)** My experience and that of many of my colleagues has been consistent over the years.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=106)** Transparent models often perform nearly as well as opaque models.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=112)** But here's the difference between what I suggest and what I observe most rookies do, however.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=119)** Don't simply give up after just one try and rush to deploy the top performer.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=125)** If an opaque model was the best performer, treat it as a pace car.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=131)** Go back to feature engineering and try to close the gap between the interpretable model and the opaque one.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=138)** You may be surprised how effective this can be.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=142)** Then even if you and your team decide that interpretable is the best option for you, that doesn't mean that you can't leverage the power of black box algorithms.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=155)** You could build a 500-tree random forest model and compare its top predictors to the ones you found in a single decision tree.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=164)** Are they the same or similar?
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=166)** That should give you greater confidence that you're on the right track.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=170)** Are they completely different?
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=172)** That's indicative of the Rashomon effect.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=175)** You should go back to exploration and data prep, specifically data reduction, and see if you can't introduce more stability into the solution.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=185)** If you want to truly understand the performance and stability of your various choices, perturb the data and try again on a different training partition.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=197)** Not only will you tend to find that performance is close across all techniques, you will also often find that the winner might change from one training partition to the next.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=210)** That's also indicative of the Rashomon effect.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=214)** It should make you more reluctant, I hope, to run something like AutoML just once and immediately deploy the first winner you find.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=224)** Interpretability or even all of the XAI techniques we've learned isn't going to help you if the patterns that you're reporting up to management were true only in that one training partition but failed to generalize to new data.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=241)** With so many options, far many more than can fit into this one course, there really is no excuse anymore to deploy an opaque model without either XAI or interpretability.
>
> **[4:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=252)** So as you navigate your options, you're choosing from interpretable or opaque with XAI.
>
> **[4:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=260)** Explanations in some form are now the requirement.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/general-advice-for-better-iml?u=76281980&t=265)** Analytics management will eventually be learning about these techniques as well, but even if they don't explicitly require them yet, due diligence now requires one of these two choices.

#### Why feature engineering is critical for IML
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/why-feature-engineering-is-critical-for-iml?u=76281980)

#### CORELS and recent trends

>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/corels-and-recent-trends?u=76281980&t=216)** But what do we make of this very tiny collection of rules?
>
> **[3:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/corels-and-recent-trends?u=76281980&t=222)** Well, if you've built a traditional decision tree, let's say using the CART algorithm, and you have five or six or seven layers in your tree and you have dozens of leaf nodes, but then you run CORELS on that same data, and you find that three or four or five rules competes with your dozens of leaf nodes, it would be indicative that some of those leaf nodes, some of those rules, in other words, in your more complex decision tree might involve a bit of noise.
>
> **[4:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/corels-and-recent-trends?u=76281980&t=255)** So what I'm suggesting is twofold.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/corels-and-recent-trends?u=76281980&t=259)** One, be on the lookout for these contemporary algorithms.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/corels-and-recent-trends?u=76281980&t=262)** There is an active research scene working on contemporary options to the problems of interpretable machine learning.
>
> **[4:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/corels-and-recent-trends?u=76281980&t=272)** Second, take an algorithm like this, even if you're not familiar with it, compare it to the results that you're getting with other algorithms.
>
> **[4:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/corels-and-recent-trends?u=76281980&t=281)** And if a very, very simple model competes with your very complex model, it does indicate that you have a bit more work to do trying to optimize your model.
>
> **[4:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/machine-learning-and-ai-foundations-producing-explainable-ai-xai-and-interpretable-machine-learning-solutions/corels-and-recent-trends?u=76281980&t=293)** So be watching for this and other contemporary algorithms.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
